**Flame Forged** — shaped by flame, they carry an echo of the departed god of fire. Their strength is in heat, their spirit is in flame — and every step they take leaves only ash behind.

- When a flame forged character deals damage with the **fire** tag, increase it by 1 for every attribute they have at a **d10 or above**.
- When they effected by **frost** tag, they become **weakened**. 

## The Talent System

Characters in Rise of Mortals grow their skills and power by gaining new talents and completing talent trees.

### Gaining talent points

Talent points are the currency used to buy talents. You earn them at the end of a session, one point per trigger — and each trigger fires **once per session**:

- You completed one of your character's goals.
- Your group completed a quest.
- You permanently lost a party member or an important NPC.
- The group defeated a villain or a boss monster.
- The group arrived at a new location.
- The group pulled off a complicated plan, or clutched a victory.

Before the adventure starts, talk with your group about your goals and your characters' motives — so the players work towards them, and the Qg writes the story around them.

If the group dislikes one or more triggers, you may drop them — a dropped trigger can never be activated by anyone in the group. **Warning:** dropping a trigger is a major decision; discuss it with every player and the Qg.

### Talent progression and renown

At **10 talent points**, and every **8 points** after that, a hero gains a new rank of **renown**:

| Renown | Rank | Talent points |
|---|---|---|
| Rookie | 0 | 0–9 |
| Adventurer | 1 | 10–17 |
| Local legend | 2 | 18–25 |
| Regional power | 3 | 26–33 |
| Kingmaker | 4 | 34–41 |
| Worldshaper | 5 | 42+ |

**A rookie lives with the following restrictions:**

- Up to **3** different talent trees.
- No attribute above a **d8**.
- No more than **2 dice** in any one attribute.
- Beginner level spells only.

Each rank of renown then lifts the ceilings:

- **Adventurer:** max dice size **d10**; up to **4** talent trees; **advanced** spells unlocked.
- **Local legend:** up to **6** talent trees; max dice number **3**; your damage reduction cap rises to **−3**; **pristine consumables** unlocked.
- **Regional power:** up to **7** talent trees; max dice size **d12**; **master** spells unlocked.
- **Kingmaker:** up to **8** talent trees; max dice number **4**; damage reduction cap rises to **−5**.
- **Worldshaper:** up to **10** talent trees; max dice number **5**; **legendary** spells unlocked.

*Important note:* some effects, items and spells boost your attributes directly — those **bypass** the maximums set by your renown.

### Spending talent points

You may spend talent points at the end of each session, in any of the following ways. One talent point buys:

- Starting a talent tree, or continuing one (see below).
- **+1 dice size** to two attributes.
- **+1 dice number** to one attribute.
- One new **beginner spell** (requires the Mana manipulator talent tree; only spells from your spell list).
- **+5** maximum mana.
- **+1** unphased.
- **+2** resilience.
- **+2** inventory points.

**Buying talents:** starting a new tree means buying its 1st talent. Within a tree you already opened, you buy strictly in order — the talent right after your latest one. Bruiser 2 unlocks Bruiser 3, never Bruiser 4.

### Talent point upgrades

When you gain the **last** talent of a talent tree, you earn one of the following benefits, based on the tree's category:

- **General combat:** +1 resilience, +2 mana, or learn a rank 1 fighting technique.
- **Weapon talent:** +1 total inventory, a rank 2 fighting technique, or 2 rank 1 fighting techniques.
- **Martial arts:** +1d4 to all hostile rolls, or a rank 1 fighting technique.
- **Magic talent tree:** +2 mana regeneration, or learn 1 beginner spell — advanced, if your renown is regional power or above.
- **Utility / travel:** +1 evasion, +2 inventory points, or +3 m movement speed.

For clarification: **spent** talent points still count towards your renown.

### Archetypes

Every talent tree belongs to one or more archetypes. They categorize the trees and hint at the playstyle each supports — but never stop you from mixing archetypes freely.

**Vanguard** — defense and protection, of yourself and others. Usually clad in heavy armor or naturally durable: tough damage dealers, or the group's outright tanks.

**Champions** — melee combatants who excel in prolonged fights: charging into hordes, or dueling elite enemies and bosses one on one. Some inflict conditions along the way, but it's rarely their core.

**Sharpshooters** — masters of ranged combat, taking out and debilitating foes with unrelenting accuracy. These trees feed ranged combat, inflicting conditions from a distance, or both.

**Commander** — strategic generals and inspiring leaders, bolstering allies through magic or sheer charisma and intellect. Commander trees favor summoners and non-magical support — but slot easily into any other archetype.

**Support** — healers, caretakers and invaluable allies: raising the group's effectiveness through magic or tender care, or granting extra abilities through cooperation.

**Mage** — proficient users of mana, capable of wondrous feats: bursts of incredible damage or elaborate defenses — though their stamina tends to run out fast.

**Versatile** — trees that benefit more than one playstyle (better movement helps everyone), or grant unique abilities that fit no archetype neatly.

**Strikers** — quick reflexes and quicker movement: first to act, hunting priority targets like enemy commanders and support. Most lack staying power, and crumble without backup.

**Controller** — fighters who cripple enemies, hit multiple foes at once, or reshape the battlefield itself. A great asset to any team — though usually short on raw stopping power.

**Unique** — a rare label, reserved for trees whose playstyle differs so fundamentally it fits no archetype at all (see: [the Qilin style](#the-qilin-style)).

## List of Talents

### Combat based talents

All of the following talent trees focus on improving a character's combat ability. They can serve outside of combat too, but they are built to sharpen hostile moves or raise a character's defenses. We recommend taking at least one or two combat trees, so your character can fight when things get tough — but a character with no combat ability whatsoever is a completely valid build.

#### General combat talents

##### The Tactician

*Commander, Support*

Leaders and commanders, able to adapt their tactics and turn any disadvantage into a winning position.

**1. Triangle strategy** — as a move on your turn, you may *change the scene* and shout one of the following commands to your allies:

- **Flank:** choose one enemy within 20 meters of you. All allies that can see that enemy may move up to 5 meters closer to it.
- **Breach:** all allies within 10 meters of you may move up to 15 meters. They can move through other creatures — but cannot end the movement sharing a space with one.
- **Assemble:** all allies that can hear you, within 30 meters, may move up to 10 meters closer to you.

Movement caused by this talent cannot be intercepted and ignores the effects of harsh terrain — but not the damage of dangerous terrain.

**2. Proper preparations** — you may spend a move on your turn and choose one of the following tactics, activating at the start of the next round. Only one can be active at a time, and it lasts until the end of that round:

- **Trade blows:** each time an ally is hit by a melee attack from within their reach, they may immediately deal 2 armor destroying damage to the attacker, adding the damage tags of a weapon of their choice they are holding.
- **Stand firm:** every ally may reduce their movement to 0 and gain −1 damage reduction.
- **Ambush:** all allies gain +1d12 on hostile rolls against unaware enemies.

**3. Crushing tactics** — once per battle, at the start of any round, you may shout the command word for the secret maneuver you went over with your team before the fight:

- **Rushdown:** all allies within 15 meters of you immediately stride.
- **Regroup:** you and all allies may each move up to half your own movement speed to a single point you choose.
- **Tactical respite:** all allies immediately clear one negative condition affecting them.

##### The Bodyguard

*Support, Vanguard*

Professionals, royal knights, or the right hand of a crime boss — these individuals specialize in protecting one, important, person.

**1. Safe keeping** — you gain a new move: **defend**. Choose an ally within your reach — they become your **ward**. Until the end of your next turn, or until they exit your reach:

- You become the target of every single-target attack, spell or ability aimed at your ward.
- Nothing can intercept your ward's actions.
- When your ward moves voluntarily, you move with them, keeping them within your reach at all times. This movement costs you no move — and can exceed your movement speed, as long as the ward stays in reach.

**2. Human shield** — once per round, when your ward starts their turn, you may transfer one negative condition affecting them onto yourself. And whenever your ward *evades*, you gain +1 evasion too.

**3. Shared suffering** — when your ward would take damage from any source, you may reduce it by the **defense value of the armor you are wearing** — before any damage reduction your ward has. After using this ability, you lose 1 resilience.

##### The Speedster

*Versatile*

This talent tree is all about movement speed and maneuverability.

**1. Runner** — +10 meters to your movement speed.

**2. Mad dash** — once per round, on your turn, you may move 10 meters in a straight line.

**3. Quick rush** — when you *stride* on your turn, until the end of your next turn:

- You can run up walls and across water, treating them as regular terrain.
- You ignore the movement cost of harsh terrain.
- You can move through other creatures' spaces (but cannot end your movement in one).

##### The Slayer

*Striker*

This talent tree is focused on attacking from stealth — and staying hidden.

**1. Skulker** — +1d10 to sense rolls made to hide, and +1d10 to attack rolls made while stealthed.

**2. Spotting weakness** *(2 points)* — you know how to read a creature mid-combat. On your turn, spend a move (or 15 seconds out of combat) to **study a creature**. When you attack a creature you studied within the last minute, you may use a fighting technique **without raising the target's evasion** — the highest technique rank this covers equals the number of moves you spent studying. You also learn a rank 1 fighting technique when you gain this talent.

**3. Spider** — when you hit a creature you used *spotting weakness* on, you may immediately apply one of:

- **Tarantula:** the creature takes +1 damage from all sources until the end of the round.
- **Trap-door** *(melee only)*: the creature is restrained until the end of your next turn. It can spend a move on a power check (test score 1) to break free — and the effect ends if it exits your weapon's reach.
- **House-jumping:** you immediately move up to 10 meters away from your target. With a melee attack, this triggers even on a miss.

##### The Raider

*Champion, Controller*

The raider is a cruel and frightening warrior, taking every opportunity to strike a weakened or impaired foe.

**1. Fear the strong** — when you knock a creature unconscious or kill it, choose a creature within 20 meters that saw it happen: it is **intimidated** by you, and the test score to remove the condition equals your **charisma dice count**. In addition, when your damage makes a creature **heavily wounded**, it is intimidated by you the same way.

**2. Exploit the weak** — against a creature with at least 1 negative condition, you gain +1d8 to attack rolls and impairing attempts. And creatures normally immune to fear treat the removal test score of *your* intimidation as 2 lower — instead of ignoring it.

**3. Dominate** — once per battle, *fear the strong* may target **any number** of creatures within a 30-meter radius, instead of one within 20.

##### The Disciple

*Versatile*

Some are naturally talented in the art of war — but learning from others can turn even the greenest warrior into a fearsome fighter.

**1. Watch and learn** — when another character makes a move, you may spend a move to **examine** it. You gain +1 success when performing a move of the same type as one you examined in the last minute (grappling, tripping, a ranged attack). To examine an attack, your weapon must share at least one trait with the weapon used in it. Only one move can be examined at a time — examining a new one drops the old.

**2. Gifted student** — the first examine of each combat costs you no move.

**3. Prediction** — intercepting a move you examined costs 1 less move.

**4. Perfect copy** — when performing a move you examined, you may replicate the examined character's roll **exactly** — including bonus dice and successes you would never normally have. Afterwards, the examine bonus for that move is spent until you examine it again.

##### The Warlord

*Champion*

Warlords fight many enemies at once, dominating battlefields with overwhelming proficiency in war.

**1. Honor in battle** — while 2 or more hostile creatures are within your melee weapon's effective reach, you gain +1 evasion and −1 damage reduction.

**2. Sweeping strike** — *whirlwind* costs you **2 moves** if it is the first move of your turn, and you may push each creature you hit with it 3 meters back.

**3. Storm of blade and hammer** — once per combat, add +2d6 to a whirlwind attack roll: every creature it hits becomes **weakened** until the end of your next turn.

##### The Bruiser

*Champion*

Bruisers specialize in close combat, squeezing every drop of potential out of short reach weapons.

**1. Close fighter** — you fight longer weapons without flinching: creatures gain no +1d6 for attacking you from outside your effective reach.

**2. Aggressive advance** — when an attack targets you from outside your effective reach, you may immediately move up to 5 meters towards the attacker — **before** the attack roll is made.

**3. Exposed shortcoming** — when you attack a creature from a distance smaller than its own maximum effective reach, its evasion and damage reduction count as 1 lower than they actually are.

**4. Pushing through** — every use of *aggressive advance* grants you 1 temporary unphased until the start of your next turn.

##### The Ronin

*Vanguard, Versatile*

Ronins practice the art of striking precisely — and surviving against overwhelming odds.

**1. Grit** — every time you take damage, you gain **grit** equal to the damage dealt. Grit is spent two ways:

- When an attack targets you: every **2 grit** spent reduces its damage by 1.
- When you make a move: every **3 grit** spent adds +1d10 to the roll.

At the end of a round in which you spent no grit, all of it disappears.

**2. Relentless spirit** — while heavily wounded, you gain 1 extra grit each time you take damage. And whenever you regain any unphased in combat, you gain 1 grit.

**3. Last stand** — once per day, if you would become **Ashen** while holding at least 5 grit, you may spend all of it to ignore all damage and effects from the source that would have sent you to the ash. After a last stand, you are immune to all damage until the end of your next turn.

**4. Warrior's spirit** — after using *last stand*, you gain 3 grit. And you start every battle with 2 grit.

##### The Grenadier

*Striker, Controller*

Nasty warriors who bring bombs, explosives and cheap tricks to a fair fight.

**1. Bombastic** — you gain a new move: **place bomb**. You set a bomb with a lit fuse in a free 1×1 meter space within 5 meters of you. The bomb starts with **2 time tokens**, and loses one whenever:

- you end your turn;
- you spend a move to shorten the fuse;
- the bomb takes damage with the *fire* tag.

At 0 tokens, it explodes: damage equal to your **intellect dice count** in a **3-meter radius** — +2 damage if your intellect is a d10 or above. Other bombs caught in the blast explode too. You can deploy a number of bombs per battle equal to your **maximum inventory points**.

**2. Backblast** — you and your allies are never damaged or affected by your own bombs. When you stand in your bomb's radius as it explodes, you may push yourself a number of meters equal to the damage you *would* have taken. Your bombs' radius grows to **5 meters**.

**3. Calculated risk** — when placing a bomb, you may **enhance** it: it now loses time tokens only when you end your turn, and it gains one damage tag of your choice, decided on placement — *fire*, *frost* (reduces the damage to 0) or *holy* (*mana drain* + inflicts *blinded*).

**4. Quick deploy** — *place bomb* now sets **2 bombs** at once, up to 10 meters away from you.

##### The Defender

*Vanguard, Controller*

Defenders are prized soldiers and mercenaries, specializing in protecting others — and drawing the enemy's attention.

**1. Tower shield** — while you have a shield without the *small* trait raised, allies within 1 meter of you gain **+1 evasion** for as long as they stay there — and can use you as **cover**.

**2. Taunting roar** — at the start of your turn, you may reduce your movement to 0 until the end of your next turn and make a **charisma roll**: for every success, you **taunt** one creature that can see or hear you.

**3. Iron defense** — creatures you taunt cannot benefit from the *armor breaker*, *armor destroyer* and *brutal* traits when attacking you.

##### The Instigator

*Support, Controller*

Some people have the skill to be just... a nuisance. Distracting their foes so badly they make the most obvious of mistakes — and leave the most vital of openings.

**1. Bratty attitude** — when you target an enemy with a hostile move or spell, or deal damage to one, you may **cancel all its damage** and **taunt** the target instead (any additional effects still apply).

- Taunts inflicted this way cannot be ignored — even by creatures normally immune to them.

**2. Obvious bait** — when a creature taunted by you targets you and you have no moves left, you may still *guard* or attempt to *intercept*. Once per enemy per battle.

**3. Bastard tactics** — allies targeting a creature taunted by you treat its evasion as 1 lower, and the creature takes **−1 on all resist rolls**.

**4. Trickster** — enemies you taunt become **tricked**:

- When you stride and end your movement within 3 meters of a tricked creature, it must spend a move to guard (if it has one available).
- When a tricked enemy attacks one of your allies, you may spend a move to call out the attack — it **misses**.
- When a tricked enemy moves towards you through the reach of one or more of your allies, one of them may make a **free hostile move** against it.

##### The Bulwark

*Vanguard*

Bulwarks are the masters of armored fighting, training their bodies to move and fight in steel.

**1. Enduring steel** — while wearing medium or low mobility armor, you gain **+1d10 to non-hostile endurance and power checks**, and creatures trying to grapple or trip you take −1 success on the roll.

**2. Unbreakable** — *armor breaker* weapons ignore only 1 point of your damage reduction, and *armor destroyer* weapons deal 1 less damage to you.

**3. Iron heart** — you gain **1 additional move** each round — usable only to *guard*.

##### The Grappler

*Champion, Controller*

Grapplers limit the opponent's movement and options — and slowly overwhelm them.

**1. Strong armed** — +1d8 to any check made to lift, pull, push, or impair a creature by restraining it. You can now stride at **full movement speed** while carrying a grappled creature.

**2. Take down** — when you start your turn with a creature grappled, you may knock it **prone** for free.

**3. Skullcrusher** — when a creature fails a power check to remove an impairment you inflicted, or when you knock a creature prone, it takes damage equal to your **power dice count** — +1 if the creature is not heavily wounded.

**4. Restrict** — when you restrain a creature with a power check, it suffers an additional **−1 evasion** and **−1 success on speed and power rolls**.

##### The Improviser

*Versatile*

Cunning and unpredictable — no plan survives an encounter with an adept improviser. They use their environment better than anyone else.

**1. Improvise** — you squeeze the utmost out of the objects (and people) around you:

- You may wield a grappled creature, or an object you're holding, as a **standard quality weapon** — its size is its reach.
- You may use a held object, or a person within 1 meter, as a **raised shield** with a defense value of 1, redirecting damage to it by the normal shield rules. Objects break on a direct hit, unless the Qg says otherwise.
- When you start your turn prone, taunted or intimidated, you may **transfer** one of those conditions to a creature within 5 meters.

**2. Adapt** — each time you use an improvised weapon, you may give it one trait of your choice: *brutal*, *deadly*, *defensive* or *thrusting*. And once per day, you *randomly find exactly what you need*: gain a common item of your choice without spending an inventory point (in combat — via *change the scene*). The item cannot cost more than 2 points; if it is a weapon, it is of poor quality.

**3. Overcome** *(2 points)* — once per round, on your turn, you may *change the scene* without spending a move. And you gain +1 success on all resist rolls.

##### The Sniper

*Sharpshooter, Versatile*

Ranged weapon purists, specializing in precise, extremely accurate shots.

- *Note: every talent in this tree also works with thrown weapons.*

**1. Steady aim** — when you are focused and steady, your shots turn deadlier: if you haven't moved since the start of your last turn, you gain **+2d6 to ranged attack rolls** until you move again.

**2. Far shot** — when shooting beyond your optimal range, you treat the target's evasion as **1 lower**.

**3. Piercing shot** — once per turn, if you have the *steady aim* bonus, your shot may punch through into a **second target** — provided it stands on the far side of the first (shooting an enemy from the front, the second target must be behind it). Use the same roll against both targets for success and damage.

##### The Shelter

*Vanguard*

Masters of battlefield awareness, proficient in turning cover and environment to their advantage.

**1. Covered movement** — when you end your turn within 1 meter of solid cover, you may enter cover **without spending a move**. If you end your turn away from any solid or abstract cover, you may move 5 meters towards the closest piece of it. And your first move after exiting cover **cannot be intercepted**.

**2. Hunker down** — the evasion bonus you gain from cover is increased by 1. When you take cover, you gain +1d10 to your next non-hostile roll — and hostile rolls made *from* cover deal **+1 damage** on a hit.

**3. Fortify** — once per round, when a creature damages you while you benefit from cover, you may reduce that damage to **1**.

##### The Dual Wielder

*Champion, Versatile*

Warriors who fight with two weapons at once — terrifying on offense and defense alike.

**1. Weapon flourish** — when you attack with one weapon while holding a second, you may make a free hostile move with the second one. Roll it as normal — but after its hit is confirmed, the free attack's base damage drops to 1.

**2. Dual wielding expert** — you can now pair **any combination** of medium and short reach weapons — and dual wield **whips and revolvers**. If your *weapon flourish* attack uses a short reach weapon, you may *guard* once for free before your next turn.

**3. Storm of blades** *(2 points)* — once per turn, spend 3 moves to make **2 attacks**, one hand and weapon per attack. Attacks made with non-short-reach weapons lose 1 success. You can still use *weapon flourish* on the same turn.

##### The Renegade

*Sharpshooter, Striker*

Quick, deadly, and always on the move. Renegades live on the edge and fight dangerously — turning the odds of battle in a split second, or losing it all in a blaze of glory.

**1. Mobile shot** — when you *stride*, you may deal **1 armor destroying damage** to a creature within your optimal range. A weapon with a reload count spends a shot on this. A *mechanical* weapon deals its mechanical score instead of 1 — but adds no other traits or damage tags.

**2. Fast hands** — if you rolled no attack during your turn, choose one effect at the start of the next round:

- reduce the reload counter of a weapon you hold by 1;
- the weapon gains +1d8 to the next hostile move made with it this round;
- +1 evasion against ranged attacks until your next turn.

**3. Daredevil** — every use of *mobile shot* or *fast hands* earns you a **daring mark**. When a round starts, you may spend **3 marks** for an **additional move**. But daring is a debt:

- If an attack hits you directly while you hold any marks, you lose them all and take 2 damage (ignoring damage reduction).
- A round without gaining a mark wipes all your marks.
- All marks vanish when you leave combat or start resting — and you cannot earn them outside of combat or genuine danger.

##### The Assassin

*Striker, Controller*

Masters of sabotage and the art of subtlety: poison, diversion and other underhanded methods — or killing the enemy before the fight even begins.

**1. Vapors** — twice per battle, when a round starts, you may throw a bomb at a point within 20 meters and line of sight:

- **Smoke bomb:** smoke spreads around cover in a 10-meter radius, creating **abstract cover** — characters can hide in it.
- **Poisonous fog:** a quickly fading cloud in a 5-meter radius: every creature inside takes 1 damage and is **poisoned**. This poison also reduces the target's power by 1 die (or to 1d4, if it would hit 0 dice) until cleared with an endurance check (test score 1).
- **Sleeping gas:** every **heavily wounded** creature within an 8-meter radius makes an endurance check (test score 2) — falling **asleep** on a failure. Ashen creatures fail automatically.

**2. Shadow touch** — you are immune to the effects of *poisonous fog* and *sleeping gas*, and can spend a move to remove the **poisoned, blinded or intimidated** condition from yourself or a creature within 1 meter — no roll needed. When you end your turn inside your smoke bomb's abstract cover, you may immediately hide (counting as 1 success rolled).

**3. Venom** — once per battle, coat your weapon — or an ally's, within 1 meter — with one oil:

- **Snake oil:** the weapon poisons targets for 1 round on hit; this poison also reduces the target's evasion by 1 on top of the usual effects.
- **Basilisk oil:** the next target hit is **blinded and restrained** (test score 1 to escape the restraint).
- **Dragon oil:** the weapon gains the *electric*, *frost* and *fire* tags on its next attack.

An oil lasts 10 minutes — but basilisk and dragon oil are spent on the first hit.

##### The Spellshot

*Sharpshooter, Mage*

Warriors who dedicate years of study to imbuing mana into bullets, arrows and bolts — granting them unique and powerful effects.

- *Special prerequisite: the talents of this tree only affect ranged attacks.*

**1. Magical bullseye** — when you make a ranged attack, you may spend **3 mana** to imbue it with one spell:

- **Fire fury:** the attack gains the *continual fire damage (2)* tag.
- **Vine spikes:** if the creature strides this round after being hit, it takes 3 damage (ignoring damage reduction) — once per stride, striding twice hurts twice.
- **Hound's chase:** your shot weaves around cover and solid surfaces: you ignore all evasion bonuses from cover, and can hit creatures behind walls — as long as they are within your optimal range.

**2. Mana nest** — when a round ends, you may spend 2 mana to create a **mana circle**, 5 meters in radius, centered on your current position. Starting your turn inside grants you 2 temporary mana, usable only for *magical bullseye* — and every ranged attack made from inside the circle deals +1 damage. The circle lasts 10 minutes, or until you make a new one.

**3. Enhanced shots** — using *magical bullseye* while standing in your mana circle, you may **dispel the circle** to upgrade the imbued spell (same 3 mana; these replace the base effects):

- **Volcanic eruption:** every creature within 5 meters of the target is knocked **prone**, and the hit applies *continual fire damage (3)*.
- **Spite curse:** every move the target takes on its next turn costs it 2 damage — and it cannot guard or evade until the end of that turn.
- **Wild hunt:** you don't roll to hit — just pick a target within optimal range. You still roll for damage.

##### The Artifact

*Striker, Mage*

Special fighters who use magical equipment in a unique way, channeling it through their weapons and strikes.

- *Special prerequisite: you must hold a spell focus to use this tree — so no two-handed weapons, and no ranged weapons.*

**1. Enchanted strikes** — when you make a weapon attack, you may add the effect of the spell focus in your hand:

- **Freeze focus:** the attack gains the *frost* tag and deals 1 less damage.
- **Flame focus:** the attack gains the *fire* tag and deals +1 damage.
- **Electric focus:** the attack gains the *electric* tag.
- **Pure focus:** the attack gains the *mana drain* tag.
- **Vampiric focus:** damaging a heavily wounded creature, or killing one, regains you 1 resilience.
- **Defensive focus:** after the attack, you gain −2 damage reduction against the next damage source that hits you before your next turn.

After enhancing an attack with any focus, you cannot enhance again for **30 seconds (2 rounds)**.

**2. Mana rush** — after landing an enhanced attack, you gain **+1 evasion and +5 meters** of movement until the end of your next turn.

**3. Mana burn** — if you start your turn with *enchanted strikes* still on cooldown, you may **buy the cooldown off** with mana: the cost is double the number of rounds remaining.

##### The Enhancer

*Champion, Mage*

Magical brutes who enchant their strikes with huge destructive power and monstrous reach.

- *Special prerequisite: you must hold a weapon in two hands to use this tree, and it cannot be a ranged weapon.*

**1. Exponential increase** — when a round starts, you may spend mana **equal to the round number**: your first hostile move this round gains **+1d6 for every point** of mana spent.

**2. Enhanced body** — every use of *exponential increase* grants you a charge of **strength**. The more strength, the more fearsome you become:

- **Muscle growth:** for every charge, your attacks gain one more trait of your choice — *brutal*, *armor breaker* or *forceful*. Once you hold all three, attacks boosted by *exponential increase* deal extra damage equal to your strength.
- **Thick skin:** for every 2 charges, you gain immunity to one of: *fire*, *frost*, *electric*, *mana drain*, *poison inflicting*, *bleed*, *weakened inflicting*.

All strength is lost when combat ends, or after 5 minutes outside of one.

**3. Magical stamina** — a hostile move affected by *exponential increase* grants you 2 temporary mana, usable only to pay for the next *exponential increase*. And when you take damage, you may reduce your **strength** instead of unphased or resilience — the excess spills into resilience.

##### The Fanatic

*Champion, Controller*

Crazed warriors who follow the way of Nihayaniran, the dead god of flame — terrorizing the battlefield with power and devotion.

**1. Praise the light!** — whenever a creature in your line of sight becomes heavily wounded, takes bleed damage, or takes damage with the *fire* tag, you gain a point of **inspiration**: each point grants **+1d4 to all your rolls**. A round in which you gained no inspiration costs you 1 point — and you can never hold more than 3.

**2. Brand the tainted!** — on your turn, spend a move and **2 inspiration** to brand a creature that damaged you last round: it is **intimidated** by you for 1 round, and every hostile move, talent and spell against it deals +1 damage.

**3. Righteous wrath!** — when you gain inspiration, or damage a branded creature, you may **taunt** any enemy that can see you. And when you take damage or a negative effect, you may spend 1 inspiration — the source of it is knocked **prone**.

##### The Cursed

*Striker*

Some are forced to bear this terrible power, some actively seek it out — the result is the same. A terrible strength flows from the curse of Nihayaniran, and those who carry it die an early death.

**1. Provoke** — if you start your turn with **0 unphased**, you may transform into your **cursed form** (the bonuses last until the end of combat):

- The transformation unleashes a terrible scream: every creature within 30 meters — allies included — is **intimidated** by you until the end of your next turn. You may repeat the scream later for 2 moves.
- Your power attacks gain *brutal*; your speed attacks gain *deadly*. If an attack already carries the trait, it gains **+1d8** to the roll instead.

**2. Tenacity** — if you took damage while transformed, then at the start of the next round: you become immune to the effects of poison and intimidation until the round ends, and you regain **1 resilience — plus 1 more for every 4 damage** you took last round.

**3. Avatar of pain** — when you become **Ashen** while transformed, you enter a ravenous rage: **+2d6 to all cinder checks**, and *tenacity* now triggers off rolling a cinder check instead of taking damage. And each time tenacity triggers while you are Ashen, instead of regaining resilience — you make **1 hostile move**.

##### The Warden

*Vanguard, Mage*

Defenders who use mana as a source of life, empowering their body and spirit.

**1. Armor of root and sap** — when your resilience would be reduced below 1, it takes no damage: instead, you reduce your **mana** by the amount you would have taken (before any resistances or reductions). At 0 mana, this cannot activate — and if you cast a spell in a round this ability triggered, it costs **double** the mana.

**2. Retaliation of thorns** — when a creature reduces your mana, it takes **armor destroying damage** equal to your charisma or intellect dice count (your choice, made when you gain this talent). Reducing your own mana never hurts you.

**3. Touch of Teragamalt** — you gain a new move, **nourish** *(2 moves)*: reduce your mana by any amount to heal another creature within 10 meters for that much **unphased**.

##### The Breaker

*Champion*

Warriors who charge head first into battle, breaking enemy lines and formations — always in the middle of the fight.

**1. Valiant charge** — once per combat, you may stride for free. This stride must end with an enemy within your reach.

**2. Glorious melee** — once per combat, when you start your turn with an enemy in reach, you may immediately attack it without spending a move. If the attack hits, you may regain 1 unphased.

**3. Press the advantage** — after an enemy moves, you may spend a move and stride, if both are true: it started its movement in your reach, and ended it outside. All movement from this stride must bring you closer to that enemy.

##### The Opportunist

*Versatile, Striker*

Quick reflexes and refined technique — negating enemy attacks and answering with devastating counters.

**1. Perfect counter** — you learn the *counter strike* fighting technique, and gain **+2d6 to interception rolls**.

**2. Quickslash** — after intercepting a creature, or guarding against its attack, you gain +1d8 on your next hostile roll against it on your next turn.

**3. Practiced parry** — after guarding, your next intercept this round costs **0 moves**.

**4. Breach and break** — when you successfully intercept a creature, it loses **all damage reduction** until the end of your next turn. When you guard against a creature, its evasion drops by 1 until the end of your next turn.

##### The Colossus

*Versatile*

Channeling the essence of the giants — carving their bodies into instruments of destruction, or growing beyond themselves towards enlightenment.

**1. Gaian might** — spend 1 move to transform into your **titan form** (it lasts as long as you like; exiting costs 1 move):

- Your **size increases by 2**; any equipment you wish to grow grows with you, proportional to your original size.
- Your melee reach with all weapons increases by 1 meter.
- +1d6 to all power rolls.
- −2 successes on sense checks made to hide, and on speed resist rolls.

**2. Strength of 100 men** — your titan form improves: size increases by **3** instead of 2; power rolls gain **1d8** instead of 1d6; and all your weapon attacks **ignore damage reduction** — attacks with *armor breaker* or *armor destroyer* gain +1 damage instead of their normal benefit.

**3. Colossus of roads** — in titan form, you gain a new move, **step through**: move up to half your movement speed (rounded down), passing through smaller creatures and solid objects — creatures you step through fall **prone**, objects are **destroyed**. You cannot end this movement sharing a space with a creature.

##### The Bastion

*Vanguard, Support*

Steadfast frontline warriors who stand against the tide — and set their allies up for unbelievable feats.

**1. Impassable sentinel** — once per turn, when a creature's stride or move would carry it into or out of your weapon's reach, you may intercept with **1 move and no check**: it stops in its tracks the moment it crosses your reach.

**2. Set up for glory** — the next hostile move an ally makes against a creature you intercepted this round gains **+1d12**.

**3. Devastating follow up** — if *impassable sentinel* stops a creature that was targeted by an ally's hostile move or spell within the last minute, it also falls **prone** and takes 1 damage.

**4. Master defender** — you gain an additional move each round, usable only for *impassable sentinel* interceptions.

##### The Trapmaster

*Versatile, Controller*

Most adventurers and monsters only think about winning once the fight has started — and never about winning it before it begins. You are not as foolish.

**1. Trapmaker** — every time you finish a rest of at least 1 hour, add **2 traps** to your inventory: tripwire or bear traps of standard quality. They take no inventory space and last until your next rest. You craft traps with focus in 5 minutes instead of 15 (always at least standard quality), place bear and tripwire traps in combat for **1 move** — and the test score for spotting your traps is 1 higher.

**2. Improved cruelty** — when placing a trap, spend one additional move to upgrade it (one upgrade per trap):

- Bear trap — **Quick fix:** counts as 1 quality rank higher; or **Complex:** the caught creature cannot succeed on the escape power check unless it focuses for 5 minutes.
- Tripwire — **Malicious:** creatures tripping the wire have their movement reduced to 5 meters until the end of their next turn; or **Arrowhead:** the creature takes damage equal to your intellect dice count from a rigged arrow, with the *armor breaker* trait.

**3. Guerrilla tactics** — a creature that activates one of your traps gains an **ambush token**: it automatically fails the next resist check it rolls within the next minute.

**4. Unseen machinations** — once per battle, when a creature activates one of your traps, you may declare it has *fallen into your trap!* — immediately place up to **7 pristine** bear or tripwire traps in a 10-meter radius around it, all hidden from that creature. (These traps are conjured by the moment, not your inventory — and cannot be retrieved afterwards. No upgrades.)

##### The Spirit Caller

*Support, Versatile*

The world of Drasil is full of natural spirits — remnants of the first great ent. Some are born connected to them, and channel them to empower their allies.

**1. Raging beasts** — when a round starts, you may spend a move to evoke an aggressive spirit onto a creature of your choice:

- **Tiger spirit:** the target deals +1 damage with attacks and spells.
- **Eagle spirit:** the target gains +1d6 to the first attack roll of its turn.
- **Bear spirit:** the target ignores all damage reduction when dealing damage.

You hold one spirit at a time — evoking a new one dissipates the old. Only one spirit can affect a creature at any time.

**2. Essence bulwark** — new, protective spirit options:

- **Rhino spirit:** the target gains −1 damage reduction, and creatures it damages are pushed 1 meter back.
- **Rabbit spirit:** when the target evades, it may stride — moving through enemies and ignoring harsh terrain.
- **Porcupine spirit:** creatures hitting the target in melee take damage equal to **your** total damage reduction.

You may now hold **2 spirits** — but must evoke them on separate rounds.

**3. Spiritual overflow** — in the first round of combat, creatures empowered by your spirits gain an **additional move**.

**4. Spirits! Gather!** — once per day, when you evoke a spirit for the second time in a fight, you may target up to **3 creatures** with it.

##### The Evoker

*Versatile, Mage, Striker*

The title of those who covet destruction in its purest form — who want to see the battlefield ruined under their influence.

**1. Ruinmaker** — when you use a damaging ability that covers an area (a line, radius or cube), you may **take damage to grow the AoE** — up to your endurance dice count, and this damage cannot be reduced. Per point taken:

- a line grows 2 meters longer, or 1 wider and taller;
- a radius grows by 1;
- a cube grows 1 on every side.

**2. Indiscriminate destruction** — when you create an AoE, pay extra mana for extra damage to everyone caught: **3 mana → +1, 5 → +2, 7 → +3**. If the ability costs no mana, you may spend 1 inventory point for +2 damage instead.

**3. The art of explosions** — every time an AoE of yours makes a creature **heavily wounded**, you become **elated**: your AoE abilities deal +1 damage, and every time an AoE damages a creature, you may move 3 meters. Elation lasts until you end a turn without damaging anyone with an AoE.

##### The Bloodfiend

*Mage, Vanguard*

Warriors who turn their own blood into a weapon — for dark rituals, and for power.

**1. Pain-packed** — as a move, give yourself **5 ranks of bleed**. Until the end of the round, every time you take damage, you gain 2 temporary resilience.

**2. Sympathetic suffering** — when you use *pain-packed*, you may enter **constant bloodloss**: whenever you take bleed damage in this state, instead of your bleed ranks dropping, the ranks of **you and every enemy within 5 meters rise by 2**. If you *hold the bleed* while in this state, constant bloodloss ends — and you lose 50% of your bleed ranks (rounded up).

**3. Traumatic transfer** — once per battle, spend a move and choose an enemy within 5 meters: it gains bleed equal to **your current bleed ranks**.

#### Weapon based talents

These talent trees have some or all of their talents tied to a specific melee or ranged weapon.

##### The Brawler

*Champion*

A talent tree focused on unarmed, hand-to-hand combat.

- *Special prerequisite: these talents are active only while you hold no weapons.*

**1. Mighty blows** — +1d10 to checks made to attack or intercept using your body — and your unarmed strikes lose the *light* trait.

**2. Beat down** — each time you make an unarmed strike, you may give it one trait of your choice: *brutal*, *forceful*, *deadly* or *armor breaker*.

**3. Master your body** — you gain a **fourth move**, usable only to:

- make an unarmed strike (this attack is *light* and deals −1 damage);
- impair a creature — prone, blinded or restrained;
- switch from one martial art stance to another (counting as both exiting the old stance and entering the new one).

##### The Fencer

*Champion, Controller*

A talent tree built on speed weaponry and defensive fighting.

- *Special prerequisite: only while holding a rapier or a parrying dagger.*

**1. Defensive duelist** — once per round, when an enemy attacks you, gain either **+1 evasion** or **−2 damage reduction** against that attack.

**2. Counteroffensive** — after *defensive duelist* helps you evade an attack or reduce its damage, your next attack roll gains **+1d6** and ignores damage reduction.

**3. Quick movement** — before or after using *defensive duelist*, or making an attack boosted by *counteroffensive*, you may move up to 3 meters towards or away from the enemy.

**4. Master duelist** — when a melee attack boosted by *counteroffensive* uses the *Feint* or *Dazing strike* fighting technique, the technique's effect triggers **even on a miss**. You also learn one of these techniques.

##### The Brute

*Champion*

Brutes maximize the power of every strike — flinging grown men across the battlefield with a single blow.

- *Special prerequisite: only for hostile moves made with a lucerne hammer, gauntlets, warhammer or mace.*

**1. Power strike** — when you attack, you may gain **+1d10** to the roll at the cost of **−1 evasion**.

**2. Proficient strength** — at the start of your turn, you may give your weapon one trait: *brutal*, *armor breaker*, *slow* or *forceful*.

**3. Pushback** — a creature hit by an attack boosted by *power strike* is pushed back a number of meters equal to the damage dealt. If a solid surface or another creature cuts the flight short, it takes damage equal to its own size.

**4. Brute force** — once per battle, before rolling a power check with a melee weapon to attack, push or intercept: you may **not roll at all** — every die you were about to roll counts as 1 success instead.

##### The Spear-Knight

*Champion*

Soldiers who mastered polearms and thrusting weapons, pressing their superior reach into every advantage.

- *Special prerequisite: only with a short-spear, war spear or lance.*

**1. Pierce** — when your melee attack enjoys the superior-reach bonus, choose one: deal 1 more damage, ignore all damage reduction, or add the **bleed** tag.

**2. Furious wave** — when a creature enters your reach, you may spend **2 moves** to make a hostile move against it.

**3. Vortex crash** — after damaging a creature with *furious wave*, you may move up to 10 meters — and, ending this movement, knock one creature within your reach **prone**.

**4. Sky breaker** — once per battle, immediately after *vortex crash* knocks a creature prone, you may attack it.

##### The Gunslinger

*Sharpshooter, Striker*

Warriors of advanced ranged weaponry, raining down hell and gunpowder.

- *Special prerequisite: only for ranged attacks with a revolver or a double barrel shotgun.*

**1. Mechanical expert** — attacks with a *mechanical* weapon gain +1d4. On a miss, the next reload of that weapon costs 1 move less.

**2. Close quarters shooter** — against creatures within your optimal range, your weapon's *mechanical* base damage rises by 1.

**3. Volley** — spend 2 moves to unleash **every bullet you have left** (a full double barrel fires 2 shots; a revolver with 3 bullets fires three). If you fired with half or more of the weapon's max ammo, every volley shot takes −1 success. *Mechanical expert*'s reload discount doesn't trigger, and volley itself needs a 1-minute cooldown.

##### The Sharpshooter

*Sharpshooter, Striker*

Accurate, deadly, precise — setting up the perfect killshot instead of attacking recklessly.

- *Special prerequisite: only while holding a bolt action rifle or a crossbow.*

**1. Deep focus** — you gain a new move, **getting in position**: your next attack roll before the end of the round gains your **sense dice**. You also enjoy this benefit while staying in solid cover.

**2. Pinpoint** — when you target a creature with a ranged attack, you may aim for a specific body part (each part works on a given creature only once per combat):

- **Center mass:** the creature gains 3 ranks of bleed.
- **Legs** *(+1 to the creature's evasion)*: on a hit, it can only stride for 5 meters of movement until the end of the round.
- **Arms** *(+2 evasion)*: on a hit, it loses motor control of one hand until the end of the round.
- **Head** *(+3 evasion)*: on a hit, it becomes **heavily wounded** until the end of the round — and if it already is, it becomes **Ashen** for the round.

**3. Killshot** — if the last move of your turn was *getting in position*, you may **mark a creature for death** (once per combat). Attacking that creature next round, your attack gains the *armor destroyer* and *bladed* traits — and *pinpoint* costs no evasion increase.

##### The Sword-Saint

*Champion, Striker*

Masters of the blade, wielding legendary techniques with explosive speed and power.

- *Special prerequisite: only when attacking with a tanto, arming sword, falchion or war sword.*

**1. Flash step** — when making a hostile move, you may spend 2 moves instead of 1 to perform a flash step: **teleport up to double your movement speed** before the attack, and gain +2d4 to the roll. You may also flash step after a successful interception by spending 1 more move — this grants the teleport only, with no attack and no bonus dice.

**2. Perfect cut** — attacking out of a flash step, you may trade one or both of its d4s for benefits:

- the attack gains *deadly* (1 die);
- the attack treats the target as **unarmored** (2 dice);
- you teleport 10 meters after the attack (1 die);
- the attack cannot be intercepted or guarded (1 die).

**3. Crestwater slash** — once per battle, when you pay for a flash step, you perform it **three times in a row**: three teleports, each followed by its own attack with its own +2d4 — and *perfect cut* may be applied to each separately.

##### The Pitcher

*Support, Striker*

Masters of thrown weapons — deadly, and creative about it.

- *Special prerequisite: only while using a throwing weapon.*

**1. Expert's mark** — after your thrown ranged attack hits a creature, it is **marked** until the end of the next round: when any attack targets it, you may consume the mark to grant that attack **+1d8**. Also, drawing a small weapon from a *bundle* no longer costs you a move.

**2. Ricochet** — if your thrown ranged attack misses, you may immediately bounce it into another creature within 5 meters of the original target. If it *hits*, you may instead choose to deal 0 damage and still ricochet to a new target within 5 meters. Either way, the new attack is a fresh roll at **−1 success**.

**3. Perfect pitch** — when your thrown weapon hits a creature marked by *expert's mark*, you may consume the mark to either **ignore all its damage reduction** or **deal double damage**. Attacks enjoying *perfect pitch* cannot apply a new expert's mark.

##### The Shieldmaster

*Vanguard, Controller*

Fighters who take shields to such a degree they become both an unbreakable wall — and a weapon that passes through any defense.

**1. Shield warrior** — improved proficiency with all shields:

- A raised **small** shield now adds its defense value against ranged attacks too.
- A **big** shield costs only 1 move to raise.
- A shield that is neither big nor small gains **+1 defensive value** in your hands.

Your shields also count as **short reach weapons with the *forceful* trait**, their weapon quality matching the shield's own. A big shield strikes at medium reach and deals +1 damage; a small one gains the *light* and *thrown* traits. And when you redirect an attack to your shield and the attacker is within the shield's reach, you may make a hostile move against them — without lowering your shield.

**2. Aggressive blocker** — after redirecting an attack to your shield, you may force the attacker to make an endurance or power check against a test score equal to your **power dice count** (+1 if your power is a d10 or above). On a failure, the attacker falls **prone**.

**3. Immovable** — if you start your turn with your shield raised, you may spend 1 move to enter a **defensive stance** until the start of your next turn: your shield stays raised no matter what, its *sturdy* score rises by 3 (or it gains *sturdy 3*), and you may redirect attacks to it an **unlimited** number of times. The price: no spells, no hostile moves on your turn.

##### The Chainmaster

*Controller, Champion*

Cunning warriors who take whips and flails to their fullest potential — a flurry of attacks that confuses the enemy.

- *Special prerequisite: only with weapons that possess the* chain *trait.*

**1. Serpent strike** — you may use the *bypass* and *bind* techniques **without raising the target's evasion**, and you learn one of them (if you know both already — any other rank 1 technique instead).

**2. Momentum strike** — if you stride before attacking on your turn, that attack gains **+1 reach** and deals 2 more damage.

**3. Enforced flex** — attacks made with *bypass* or *bind* gain an extra effect:

- **Bypass:** push the creature 1 meter back and knock it **prone**.
- **Bind:** pull the creature up to 2 meters closer and **taunt** it.

**4. Heavenly chains** — once per turn, when *enforced flex* lands, you may **double** the distance you move the creature — and it takes **−2 evasion** until it takes damage or your next turn ends.

##### The Bloodletter

*Champion*

Bloodletters are brutal and efficient warriors, achieving great feats in battle while lost to bloodlust.

- *Special prerequisite: only with a bearded axe, halberd or glaive.*

**1. Massacre** — you learn the *draw blood* technique. When you hit a creature that already has at least 1 rank of bleed, you may raise its bleed by 2.

**2. Bloodlust** — when a creature in your line of sight takes **bleed damage**, you may move up to your movement speed towards it. This movement cannot be intercepted.

**3. Exsanguinate** — once per battle, when you damage a heavily wounded creature with at least 1 rank of bleed, note its current bleed ranks: your next attack to hit before the end of the next round inflicts **that much bleed** on whatever creature it strikes.

##### The Juggernaut

*Champion or Sharpshooter (depends on the weapon)*

Unmatched powerhouses of destruction — a juggernaut can single-handedly take down buildings and walls.

- *Special prerequisite: only with weapons that carry the* slow *trait.*

**1. Powerhouse** — your slow-weapon attacks may **ignore any solid cover or wall** between you and the target — the strike simply shatters through. Whenever you hit a piece of solid cover, or smash through one this way, it **explodes**: 2 damage to everyone within a 1-meter radius, and a 1×1 meter piece of the cover is destroyed.

**2. Slow start** — if you *wind up* on a turn you didn't attack, then until you strike with the slow weapon or end your next turn: your damage reduction and evasion **cannot be reduced or ignored**, and you **do not count as heavily wounded**.

**3. Rebound** — when you end a turn in which you attacked with a slow weapon, you may *wind up* without spending a move.

**4. Meteor** — when you start your turn with a slow weapon ready to strike, you may move up to half your movement speed (rounded up).

##### The Engineer

*Sharpshooter, Controller*

Sharpshooters and creative geniuses, chasing the perfect balance between the mechanical power of guns and the versatility of the bow.

- *Special prerequisite: these talents only affect the hand crossbow and the sling.*

**1. Star surprise** — when you rest, you may use *craft an item* and spend any number of inventory points: each point yields **two uses** of a special ammo of your choice. Spend a use before an attack roll to add its effect:

- **Venom star:** on a hit, the target is poisoned until the end of its next turn — and takes −1 on resist rolls while poisoned this way.
- **Exploding star:** the target and everyone within 3 meters take 1 fire damage.
- **Sticky star:** the target is restrained until the next round (test score 1 to escape).

**2. Workshop** — while camping, use *craft an item* to enhance your weapon with **2** upgrades:

- **Aim assist:** the weapon's optimal range grows by +1 sense die.
- **Quickfire:** each hostile move against a character lets you roll one **additional attack** against them, dealing the weapon's minimum damage (1, unless it is *mechanical*).
- **Powershots:** the weapon gains *mechanical (2)* — or +2 to an existing mechanical score — and the *deadly* trait.

**3. Grand design** — *workshop* now installs up to **3 upgrades**, including **supreme** ones at 2 slots each:

- **Artillery:** +100 meters of maximum range, +1 damage.
- **Compatible:** fighting techniques raise the target's evasion by just **1**, regardless of rank.
- **Synergy rounds:** apply **2 ammo types** from *star surprise* to one attack (one use of each) — or double down on the same type:
  - 2 venom stars — the poison lasts 1 minute;
  - 2 exploding stars — everyone taking the fire damage is knocked prone;
  - 2 sticky stars — the target also loses 1 move on its next turn.

##### The Marksman

*Sharpshooter, Striker*

Archers — fast, accurate, and able to target multiple foes with ease.

- *Special prerequisite: only with a shortbow or a longbow.*

**1. Multi-shot** — when firing a ranged attack, you may target up to **three different creatures** within range, spending one additional move per target beyond the first. All these attacks gain the *light* trait.

**2. Arching shot** — your ranged attacks ignore the evasion bonus of **solid cover** (line of sight still required). And you may take −1 success on a ranged attack roll to give it *armor breaker* and **double its maximum range**.

**3. Triple strike** — your *multi-shot* attacks no longer gain the *light* trait. And once per combat, *multi-shot* may target the **same enemy** with all its attacks.

##### The Virtuoso

*Champion, Striker, Controller*

A master of self-defense and non-lethal strikes, practicing a complex fighting style called **the performance** — dance-like, beautiful, and brutally efficient.

- *Special prerequisite: only with a fighting staff — and the damage from these talents can never reduce a creature's resilience or unphased to 0.*

**1. Entrance** — when a battle starts, you may immediately stride, evade, or prepare to intercept (your first interception of the combat costs no move). And the first time each round a creature **misses** you with an attack, you may make a hostile move against it — to blind, trip or strike.

**2. Chorus** — the first time each round you try to attack, trip or blind a creature, you gain a **free move**, usable only to attack, trip or blind a *different* creature (it doesn't count against your hostile moves this turn). And whenever you blind or trip a creature by any means, you may move up to 5 meters.

**3. Finale** — every hostile move made through *entrance*, and every free move from *chorus*, earns you a stack of **finale**. Once per combat, when a round ends, spend all your stacks on one ending:

- **Tragedy:** you take damage equal to your finale stacks — this damage cannot be reduced or prevented in any way. Your next hostile move gains that many **d10s** — and this one attack can reduce a creature to 0 resilience.
- **Hopeful:** for a number of rounds equal to your stacks, you regain 1 unphased at the start of each of your turns.
- **Inspiring:** all allies who can see or hear you gain bonus movement equal to your stacks until the end of the next round, and +1d12 to their next check.
- **Terrifying:** all enemies who can see or hear you are **intimidated** by you for half your stacks in rounds (rounded up).

You lose all finale stacks if a full round passes without gaining a new one.

##### The Artillerist

*Sharpshooter, Controller*

The finest mechanics of the modern age created something magnificent in the hand mortar — and you intend to put it to good use.

- *Special prerequisite: only with a hand mortar, or any siege weapon you happen upon.*

**1. Howitzer** — when your hand mortar or siege weapon damages a creature, you may knock it **prone**. And prone creatures get **no resist roll** against your hand mortar and siege weapon attacks.

**2. Rocket rider** — when you fire a hand mortar or siege weapon, pick one:

- reduce the weapon's reload count by 2;
- the attack ignores cover;
- the attack gains the *explosive* enchantment.

**3. Booming terror** — once per combat, when your hand mortar or siege weapon damages creatures, you may declare a booming terror: every damaged creature is **intimidated** by you (test score 3 to remove), loses **5 unphased** and **1 resilience** — plus 2 more of each per quality rank of your weapon above standard.

##### The Impaler

*Champion, Controller*

Brutal warriors who skewer their enemies with merciless efficiency, using the ungodly reach of their pikes to bully and stab.

- *Special prerequisite: only with a pike.*

**1. Tormentor** — when you attack with the pike, you may choose to **skewer**: the attack gains the *bleed* tag, and on a hit the creature is skewered — its movement drops to 0, and it gains 1 bleed rank at the start of each of its turns. Being skewered ends when the creature spends a move to *change the scene* and pull the pike out, when it exits your reach, or when you release it at the start of your turn. You cannot attack with the pike while a creature hangs on it.

**2. Tepesh** — a creature that stops being skewered takes damage equal to its **current bleed ranks**. And while skewering, you may spend a move to **twist the pike**, adding bleed ranks equal to your power dice count.

**3. Human spire** — while within 1 meter of a creature skewered by you, you may spend 2 moves to **impale** it: you plant the pike in the ground, piercing the creature through. It becomes **restrained** and immediately gains **5 bleed ranks** — and it cannot free itself (unless it can fly): another creature must spend 2 moves on a power check (test score 2) to pull it off. You don't need to keep holding the pike of an impaled creature.

#### Martial art talents

Martial art talents are focused on unarmed combat and the perfection of technique.

**Unique feature — the battle stance.** Every martial art tree has a stance, gained with the tree's first talent:

- Entering a stance costs **1 move** — and you cannot use a tree's talents without entering its stance first.
- You cannot hold two stances at once.
- Exiting a stance is a **free move** — but you cannot exit and enter the same stance in one round.
- Becoming **Ashen** throws you out of your stance.

##### The Storm Style

*Champion*

The most destructive martial art still practiced in modern times — its users release enough energy to shatter boulders and bones with ease.

**Stance — Typhon:** you may add the *slow* trait to all your melee attacks.

**1. Lightning** — if you wound up a slow attack on your last turn, your movement speed is **doubled until the end of your next turn**. And whenever you wind up, you may deal 2 armor destroying damage to every creature within your weapon's melee reach.

**2. Thunder** — when you attack with the *slow* trait, every creature in a 5-meter radius **behind the target** takes 3 damage.

**3. Echo** — all damage from *lightning* and *thunder* gains the *electric* tag. Creatures damaged by them are **marked by the storm** — and when you exit your stance, every marked creature takes 1 electric damage.

##### The Gust Style

*Vanguard, Striker*

Focused on evading attacks and redirecting harm — favored by pacifists, and by the extremely battle-hungry.

**Stance — Whirlwind:** when you enter this stance, and whenever a round starts while you are in it, you may pull one hostile creature 5 meters horizontally closer to you.

**1. Breath** — while in this stance, +1 evasion against creatures you forcefully moved this round.

**2. Gale** — you release the gathered energy in a single strike. Gale becomes available after using *breath*, and triggers when you land an unarmed strike or intercept an attack: every enemy within 3 meters is pushed back a number of meters equal to the **dice you rolled** for the attack or interception, and the creature you hit or intercepted becomes **weakened** until the end of its next turn. Exiting the stance resets the sequence — *breath* first, then *gale*.

**3. Breeze** — after using *breath*, your senses sharpen: for the rest of the battle (or until you exit the stance), whenever an enemy **misses** you, you may counter for X armor destroying damage — X being your speed or power dice count, whichever is higher. This ends early when you use *gale*. Also, creatures pushed by your gale now take 2 armor destroying damage.

##### The Sand Style

*Champion, Controller*

Sand style users are tricksters, ready to do anything to win — dirty tricks and dishonorable tactics, all for the advantage.

**Stance — Shifting:** entering or exiting this stance at the start of your turn is **free**. On entering, you may immediately make an unarmed strike that automatically **misses**; on exiting, you may move up to 5 meters.

**1. Blinding strike** — when your unarmed strike misses a creature, you may **blind** it. You must exit the stance before using this again.

**2. Mirage** — you've learned to fight the impaired so well they cannot touch you: attacks from **weakened or blinded** creatures against you automatically miss.

**3. Cheap strike** — when a creature misses you within your reach, you may deal it 1 damage. And your damage against weakened or blinded opponents **cannot be reduced**.

##### The Mountain Style

*Champion*

Also called the "gaian style" — famous for its abnormal reach, and for practitioners who can, sometimes literally, split mountains.

**Stance — Bedrock:** your charged attacks deal extra damage equal to **a third of their reach** (rounded up).

**1. Stone-edge** — spend a move to **charge** your next strike: it gains 2 more meters of reach and the *forceful* trait. If it already had *forceful*, every die rolled counts towards the trait (treat an attack with no power dice as having 1). You take 1 damage after landing a charged attack.

**2. Rockslide** — the first time each round you charge an attack, your next move that turn is enhanced:

- **Stride:** costs 1 less move, and you pass through creatures as if they were harsh terrain.
- **Evade:** costs 1 less move, and you deal 1 damage to everything within your reach.
- **Intercept:** costs 1 less move, and gains +2d6.

**3. Summit splitter** — you may charge an attack **any number of times**, stacking the reach increase — though reach stops growing after the 5th charge. The charges bring milestones:

- **2+ charges:** the strike deals 2 armor destroyer damage to the target *before* the roll to hit.
- **4+ charges:** the strike hits every creature in a straight line within its reach.
- **7+ charges:** the knockback from *forceful* is tripled.
- **10+ charges:** the strike deals an additional **30 damage** on a hit.

##### The River Style

*Champion, Striker*

Focused on overwhelming an enemy — weakening them under a rain of strikes.

**Stance — Waterfall:** when your speed-based unarmed strike hits, you may attack the target again **for free** — but its evasion rises by 2 for every previous hit you landed this turn. Hits from the stance's free attacks trigger it again. The evasion increase resets at the end of each turn.

**1. Flowing offense** — creatures within 1 meter of you have their evasion reduced by 1. This cannot bring evasion to 0 — unless the creature is heavily wounded or Ashen.

**2. Overwhelming current** — when your unarmed strike hits, you may increase its damage by the number of times you already damaged that creature this round. Afterwards, *waterfall stance* is spent until the next round.

**3. Clashing ocean** — the first time each round one of the following happens, you may make a **free unarmed attack** against the creature in question:

- you stride and end your movement within 1 meter of a creature;
- a creature ends its turn within 1 meter of you;
- a creature within 1 meter of you is inflicted with a negative condition.

##### The Flower Style

*Striker, Versatile*

Deadly, accurate and fast — renowned for elegant, delicate strikes and a specialty in one-on-one combat.

**Stance — Thorn:** the first time each round you inflict bleed on a creature, you mark it with **thorns**: a thorned creature's bleed ranks no longer drop when it takes bleed damage — only when it *holds the bleed*.

**1. Daisy step** — spend a move to enter **daisy step**: until the end of the round, whenever a creature ends its turn, you may move 5 meters in a straight line.

**2. Rose cut** — while *daisy step* is active, ending any instance of movement within 1 meter of a creature lets you give it **1 bleed rank**.

**3. Blossoming blade** — when a round ends, you may spend 2 moves to attack **every thorned creature within 10 meters**: roll separately against each target, adding a d6 for every bleed rank that target has. Each target hit then clears all its bleed.

##### The Wildfire Style

*Champion, Striker*

Indiscriminate destruction — the users of this rare style are known for the collateral damage they leave behind.

**Stance — Ember:** all your unarmed strikes gain the *fire* tag.

**1. Pillar of flames** — when your turn starts, you may explode: take any amount of damage (up to your unphased score) that cannot be reduced in any way — and every creature within a **radius equal to that damage** takes the same amount, with the *fire* tag.

**2. Eternal flame** — creatures damaged by your *pillar of flames* (yourself included) gain a **mark of ashes**: the next time that creature would take damage, the damage is cancelled, the mark burns away — and the creature gains continual fire damage equal to the cancelled amount.

**3. Burn it all** — when your turn ends, you may spend a move to **extinguish** any number of creatures in your line of sight that are under continual fire damage: they lose all of it — and every creature within 3 meters of each extinguished one takes 2 fire damage.

##### The Forest Style

*Vanguard, Support*

The most ancient style still alive in Drasil — unwavering defense, and the support of others.

**Stance — Oak:** whenever your movement is reduced in any way, you gain −1 damage reduction and +1d8 to all power, endurance and willpower checks.

**1. Sturdy trunk** — when your turn starts, you may root yourself: your movement drops to 0, and until the start of your next turn you **cannot be moved, pushed or grappled** — nor can you leave the spot willingly.

**2. Engulfing branch** — while *sturdy trunk* is active, your reach grows by **3 meters**, and allies within 3 meters of you count as having **abstract cover**.

**3. Falling leaves** — whenever your movement is reduced, you may grant a creature you can see within your weapon's reach bonus movement equal to what you lost.

##### The Snow Style

*Controller*

Silent, soft and cold — small movements, delicate strikes, and enemies suffocating in a slow death.

**Stance — Avalanche:** once per round, when you reduce a creature's movement, it takes 1 damage per 5 meters reduced. This damage cannot be reduced in any way.

**1. Encroaching frost** — spend a move to raise a **frost aura**: 5 meters in radius, moving with you. Attacks targeting creatures inside the aura gain the *frost* tag.

**2. Ice field** — your aura counts as **harsh terrain** (not for you). A creature starting its turn inside while affected by frost takes 1 frost damage.

**3. Snowflake** — when a creature inside your aura uses *change the scene* to remove its movement reduction, you may place a **snowflake token** on it: if the creature moves at all, the token is consumed, and at the end of its movement it takes **1 damage per meter moved**. A turn spent perfectly still lets the token fade harmlessly.

##### The Dragon Style

*Champion, Versatile*

A whirlwind of blades, arrows and hammers — masters of every weapon, switching them at a moment's notice.

**Stance — Wyvern:** at the start and end of your turn, you may switch one melee weapon you are holding. Any switch made through this stance or the style's talents must be to a weapon of a **different reach**.

**1. Claw** — whenever you switch weapons (via *change the scene* or the stance), you may immediately deal **1 damage** to a creature within the new weapon's reach. This damage takes no bonuses or tags, cannot reduce anyone to 0 resilience or unphased, and triggers no fighting techniques.

**2. Fang** — when you make a hostile move, stride or evade, you may immediately switch one melee weapon and use *claw*.

**3. Wing** — *claw* may trade its damage for one of:

- the target is pushed 2 meters back;
- you immediately move up to 3 meters (uninterceptable);
- the target loses 1 success from its next check (doesn't stack).

##### The Demon Style

*Champion*

A sadistic and cruel style, known for draining the life force of the user — and of everyone else.

**Stance — Crimson:** you lose 1 resilience at the end of every round — and your first unarmed strike each round gains the *draining* tag.

**1. Transfusion** — when your draining attack hits, pick one effect (each can be chosen only once per round):

- the attack also gains the *bleed* tag;
- the creature cannot regain resilience or unphased until the start of your next turn;
- you regain unphased equal to the damage dealt.

**2. Sanguine pool** — once per battle, when you lose at least 1 unphased or resilience, you may deal **1 draining damage to everything within 10 meters** — becoming weakened until the end of your next turn.

**3. Toxic hemorrhage** — creatures damaged by your *draining* attacks are **poisoned** until the end of their next turn.

##### The Qilin Style

*Champion, Unique*

Patience is a virtue, and Qilin practitioners take it to heart: they draw power from their surroundings — and unleash it only at the right moment.

**Stance — Cerulean:** at the start of each round in this stance, you **lose 1 move and gain 1 rank of stockpile**. All stockpile disappears 5 minutes after your first rank, or when you exit the stance.

**1. Event horizon** — every rank of stockpile adds **3 meters** to your movement; every 2 ranks add **+1d6** to all your hostile and resist rolls.

**2. Power storage** — when you end your turn, you may spend 3 mana for 1 rank of stockpile.

**3. Teal surge** — spend 1 move to wind up your entire stockpile, as with any *slow* weapon — the strike must be the **first move of your next round**, or you exit the stance. The strike:

- has reach equal to the stockpile spent;
- gains **+1d12** per rank;
- is based on no attribute, and carries *armor destroyer*, *forceful*, *brutal* and *slow*.

##### The Demiurge Style

*Striker, Champion*

The only style forbidden across all of Drasil: its users are hunted down and killed in every civilized land — for this style attacks the mind instead of the body, and for the untold suffering it brings.

**Stance — Supreme ruler:** the second attack you make each round gains *armor destroyer* — if it is made with an unarmed strike or a **poor quality weapon**.

**1. Pale cloud** — once per round, when you stride, you may make a free attack against a creature that was within your reach at any point of the movement. *Pale cloud* can only reduce **unphased**, never resilience.

**2. Dark bolt** — at the start of a round, spend 1 move to prepare. When the round ends, you send a forcewave down a straight line, 1 meter wide and 20 long: choose a number from 1 to 3 — every creature caught **loses that much resilience and gains that much temporary unphased**.

**3. Soul-cutting uncertainty** — once per combat, when a round starts, you may attack a creature that has at least 1 point of unphased or temporary unphased. Roll an attack with one of your weapons, ignoring its quality. This unique attack has no reach or range, cannot be redirected or intercepted, and carries no traits. The target counts as having **0 evasion and 0 damage reduction**, and cannot change either until the attack resolves. A creature that takes even 1 damage from it is **weakened, blinded and intimidated** by you — all lasting until the end of your next turn, and none removable before that.

##### The Shadow Style

*Vanguard, Controller*

When the old shadow style fell to a rogue mage, it was reformed — into a style of defense and anti-magic.

**Stance — Shade:** when your turn starts, you may immediately evade, or clear one negative condition on you. Using this forbids you from making hostile moves and from starting, continuing or finishing a spell this turn.

**1. Simple moon** — when you evade, you may assume the **simple moon guard**, held until you move, are moved, or make a hostile move. While holding it, the first time an enemy enters your reach, you may immediately attack it — this attack gains *armor destroyer*.

**2. Dark horizon** — while in *simple moon guard*, if you are targeted by — or caught in the area of — a spell or mana-spending ability, you may exit the *simple moon guard* and **cancel the triggering spell or ability**. You take 1 damage and become weakened until the start of your next turn.

**3. Quick midnight** — attacking through *simple moon*, or using *dark horizon*, earns you a charge of **midnight**. Spend a charge when attacking to strike at the creature's **base evasion**, ignoring every increase and decrease — or spend it on a hit to **end one non-permanent effect** on the target.

##### The Autumn Style

*Champion, Controller*

A style practiced by the pacifist monks of the far west — a variation of the gust style that is more active and decisive.

**Stance — White chain:** when you push an enemy back, you place a **vigilant gaze** mark on it. A creature holds only 1 mark at a time.

**1. Heart of the unrepented** — when you end your turn within 1 meter of a hostile creature, you may push it 5 meters back. If it bears a *vigilant gaze* mark, it is also **poisoned** (−1 to all rolls on top of the usual effects) — and the poison only ends when the creature finishes a turn without moving.

**2. Vengeful iron** — when a melee attack hits you, you may push the attacker back until you stand 1 meter outside its reach (after the hit resolves). If it bears a mark — it also takes 2 damage and falls **prone**.

**3. 47 empty palms** — when your unarmed strike hits, you may push the target a number of meters equal to its size. If it bears a mark — it is instead pushed **until it hits a wall**, an object of its size, or a creature of equal or greater size, taking 3 damage that cannot be reduced in any way.

##### The Shooting Star Style

*Sharpshooter*

Streaking through the battlefield like a star across the clear night sky — practitioners of this style paint art with their arrows and bullets.

**Stance — Southern star:** when your ranged attack hits a creature, you may mark it as a **star node**. You always count as a star node yourself — and may spend a move to mark a size 1 space within your optimal range as one. Nodes fade after 10 minutes.

**1. Eastern sunrise** — once per round, spend 1 move to draw a straight **line between two star nodes** (1 meter wide, no passing through objects): every creature it crosses takes 2 damage. With more than 2 nodes on the field, you may repeat this **for free** — each new line must start where the last ended, and cannot return to a node already connected this round.

**2. Western sunset** — when a round starts, you may **dim** all current star nodes in line of sight. At the round's end, every dimmed node **shines bright**, blinding all creatures within 1 meter of it — creatures that *are* nodes included (you too). Nodes created this round start dimmed.
